<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_information">Team information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Team information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jerseys">Jerseys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Jerseys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original 1972 design featured the now-traditional colours of blue and orange, but reversed from their more familiar appearance in later seasons, orange being the dominant colour and blue used for the trimming. For the first few games of the 1972 season, player names were not displayed on the uniform; rather the word "ALBERTA" was written in that space. About halfway through the season, though, the player names made their appearance, since the Oilers had played exclusively in Edmonton.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> These jerseys also featured the player numbers high on the shoulders, rather than on the upper sleeve.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1975%E2%80%9376_WHA_season" title="1975–76 WHA season">1975–76 season</a>, the jersey was changed to a blue base with orange trim. The logo that appeared on programs and promotional material remained the same. However, the logo that appeared on the home jersey had a white oil drop, on a dark orange field, with the team name written in deep blue. The away jersey featured an orange-printed logo.</p>
<p>When the team joined the NHL in 1979, the alternate logos were discarded, giving the jersey its most famous form. However, the logo appeared slightly differently on a few vintages of the jersey. Minor changes were also made to the numbering, lettering and collar in their first few NHL campaigns. From 1982 to 1989, <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> provided the Oilers' sweaters.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/ff/Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg/150px-Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg.png" width="150" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/ff/Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg/225px-Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/ff/Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg/300px-Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_Edmonton_Oilers_Alternate.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Edmonton's former alternate logo, former primary used from 1996 to 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The essential design remained untouched until 1996, when the team colours were changed to midnight blue and copper with red trim. Other changes made to the jersey at that point were the removal of the shoulder bar and cuffs from the away jersey, and the addition of the "Rigger" alternate logo to the jersey's shoulders. A year later, the shoulder bars were removed from the home jersey as well, and the Oilers' sweater design then remained stable until 2007.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg/150px-EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg.png" width="150" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg/225px-EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f1/EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg/300px-EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="216" data-file-height="157" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EdmontonOilersAlternate.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Edmonton's former alternate logo, used from 2001 to 2007. A raining drop of oil surrounded by half of a sprocket and metal; designed by <a href="/wiki/Spawn_(comics)" title="Spawn (comics)">Spawn</a> creator and former Oilers co-owner <a href="/wiki/Todd_McFarlane" title="Todd McFarlane">Todd McFarlane</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2001, the Oilers introduced their first alternate <a href="/wiki/Third_jersey" title="Third jersey">third jersey</a>. Designed by then-minority owner <a href="/wiki/Todd_McFarlane" title="Todd McFarlane">Todd McFarlane</a> and his production studio, the new uniforms were a radical departure from previous Oilers designs. The original Oilers logo was completely absent, along with copper and red; midnight blue was complemented with two shades of silver/grey, and the primary logo was a flying set of gears with an oil drop on top. Elements of the logo paid tribute to the five Stanley Cup titles and ten team captains to that point. A silver shield bearing "OILERS" above a variation of the oil-drop gear adorned the shoulders.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> The jersey's sleeve numbers are located inside the white sleeve stripe.</p>
<p>In 2007, with the NHL's switch to <a href="/wiki/NHL_uniform#Since_2007:_Reebok_Edge" title="NHL uniform">Reebok Edge</a> jerseys, the Oilers kept their team colours but changed the style of their jerseys. Most notable about the Edge jerseys were the removal of the waistline stripes in favour of vertical piping, and the sleeve stripes only appearing on the inside of the elbow panels. The "Rigger" was retired, along with the McFarlane third jersey and its associated logos.</p>
<p>In 2008, the Oilers introduced a new alternate jersey that closely resembled the blue-and-orange away jersey of the dynasty era. For the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_NHL_season" title="2009–10 NHL season">2009–10 season</a>, this jersey became the Oilers' main home jersey as blue and orange became the primary team colours once again. The old midnight blue-and-copper jersey became their alternate. On June 24, 2011, the Oilers presented their new white road jerseys at the 2011 NHL Entry Draft, when they selected Ryan Nugent-Hopkins first overall.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The midnight blue jersey remained as the third jersey before being dropped altogether in 2012.</p>
<p>The Oilers unveiled a new alternate jersey prior to the 2015–16 season. The uniform closely resembled the team's original orange uniform from their WHA days.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Oilers mascot is a <a href="/wiki/Canada_lynx" title="Canada lynx">Canadian Lynx</a> named Hunter. He was unveiled on September 26, 2016.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oilers_Octane">Oilers Octane</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Oilers Octane">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Oilers_Octane" title="Oilers Octane">Oilers Octane</a></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_NHL_season" title="2010–11 NHL season">2010–11 season</a>, the Oilers introduced the <a href="/wiki/Oilers_Octane" title="Oilers Octane">Oilers Octane</a>, the first cheerleading squad for a Canadian NHL team. The Oilers Octane consists of 19 women aged 18 to 29, most of whom are from the greater Edmonton area (within neighbouring suburbs), or the province of Alberta.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The cheer team was, initially, not greeted with enthusiasm by all fans. Just over 1,500 people signed an online petition against it, suggesting the women do not improve the game experience and may in fact hinder it. Many felt the cheer team was a cheap <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> stunt and considered it disrespectful to women and completely unrelated to hockey.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to performing cheers at Oilers home games, helping with promotions and interacting with fans, the Octane members participate in charity fund raising and special events.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2016 the Oilers announced they were discontinuing the Octane cheer team as they moved to their first season in the new <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Place" title="Rogers Place">Rogers Place</a> arena, as well as announcing auditions for a new Oilers Orange and Blue Ice Crew "brand ambassador' group.<sup id="cite_ref-Octane2016_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Octane2016-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_records">Franchise records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Franchise records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scoring_leaders">Scoring leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Scoring leaders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Single-season_leaders">Single-season leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Single-season leaders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<p>Items marked in <b>bold</b> are NHL records.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>Most goals in a season: <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky" title="Wayne Gretzky">Wayne Gretzky</a>, 92 (1981–82)</b></li>
<li><b>Most assists in a season: <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky" title="Wayne Gretzky">Wayne Gretzky</a>, 163 (1985–86)</b></li>
<li><b>Most points in a season: <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky" title="Wayne Gretzky">Wayne Gretzky</a>, 215 (1985–86)</b></li>
<li>Most penalty minutes in a season: <a href="/wiki/James_Stephen_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="James Stephen Smith">Steve Smith</a>, 286 (1987–88)</li>
<li><b>Most goals in a season, defenceman: <a href="/wiki/Paul_Coffey" title="Paul Coffey">Paul Coffey</a>, 48 (1985–86)</b></li>
<li>Most points in a season, defenceman: <a href="/wiki/Paul_Coffey" title="Paul Coffey">Paul Coffey</a>, 138 (1985–86)</li>
<li>Most goals in a season, rookie: <a href="/wiki/Jason_Arnott" title="Jason Arnott">Jason Arnott</a>, 33 (1992–93)</li>
<li>Most assists in a season, rookie: <a href="/wiki/Jari_Kurri" title="Jari Kurri">Jari Kurri</a>, 43 (1980–81)</li>
<li>Most points in a season, rookie: <a href="/wiki/Jari_Kurri" title="Jari Kurri">Jari Kurri</a>, 75 (1980–81)</li>
<li>Most wins in a season: <a href="/wiki/Grant_Fuhr" title="Grant Fuhr">Grant Fuhr</a>, 40 (1987–88)</li>
<li>Most shutouts in a season: <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Joseph" title="Curtis Joseph">Curtis Joseph</a>; <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Salo" title="Tommy Salo">Tommy Salo</a>, 8 (1997–98; 2000–01)</li>
</ul>
</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_arenas">Home arenas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Home arenas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Edmonton_Gardens" title="Edmonton Gardens">Edmonton Gardens</a> 1972–1974</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Northlands_Coliseum" title="Northlands Coliseum">Northlands Coliseum</a> 1974–2016</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Stadium_(Edmonton)" title="Commonwealth Stadium (Edmonton)">Commonwealth Stadium</a> (<a href="/wiki/2003_Heritage_Classic" title="2003 Heritage Classic">2003 Heritage Classic</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rogers_Place" title="Rogers Place">Rogers Place</a> 2016–present</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasters">Broadcasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Edmonton_Oilers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Broadcasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/250px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png" width="250" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/375px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg/500px-Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1353" data-file-height="1272" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rogers_Sportsnet_Regions.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Edmonton Oilers broadcast area in orange, but its coverage is blacked out in Manitoba.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In addition to the national coverage of the Oilers on <i><a href="/wiki/NHL_on_Sportsnet" title="NHL on Sportsnet">NHL on Sportsnet</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hockey_Night_in_Canada" title="Hockey Night in Canada">Hockey Night in Canada</a></i>, the regional coverage of the games are aired on television live on <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet" title="Sportsnet">Sportsnet West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sportsnet_One" title="Sportsnet One">Sportsnet Oilers</a> with its on air staff <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Quinn_(sportscaster)" title="Kevin Quinn (sportscaster)">Kevin Quinn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drew_Remenda" title="Drew Remenda">Drew Remenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gene_Principe" title="Gene Principe">Gene Principe</a>. Like the <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Flames" title="Calgary Flames">Calgary Flames</a>, those games are available in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">Saskatchewan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Territories" title="Northwest Territories">Northwest Territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nunavut" title="Nunavut">Nunavut</a>.</p>
<p>On radio, the games are aired on <a href="/wiki/CHED_(AM)" title="CHED (AM)">CHED</a> called by Jack Michaels and Bob Stauffer and Reid Wilkins as reporter. Tom Gazzola is the reporter for the Oilers online.</p>
